        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Blash blasted 32 homers in the minors in 2015, which prompted the Padres to snag him in the rule 5 draft. His success didn't translate to the big leagues, however, and he wound up spending most of the year back at Triple-A. Blash has always oozed flashy tools and still does: he has tremendous raw power, he runs well and has a strong throwing arm. But his swing features a very deep load that is easily exploited by big league pitching. In other words, he's missing that all-important hit tool. Considering he's already 27, it's unlikely Blash will be able to make the necessary adjustments. He might carve out a niche as a power-only bench bat, or maybe occupy the short side of a platoon, but he'll almost certainly never be a regular. <a href="https://twitter.com/_chris_mitchell">(Chris Mitchell)</a><br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Blash destroys minor league pitching, but at age-27, he's yet to succeed in the show. He'll probably get another chance or two, but don't count on much production.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
